   {
					"@context": "http://schema.org",
					"@type":"Article",
					"url": "http://www.huffingtonpost.com/2014/08/14/media-black-victims_n_5673291.html",
            		"author": {
                "@type":"Person",
                "name":"Nick Wing"
				},
					"headline": "When The Media Treats White Suspects And Killers Better Than Black Victims",
					"articleBody": "On the afternoon of Aug. 9, a police officer fatally shot an unarmed, black teenager, Michael Brown, in Ferguson, Missouri. Details remain in dispute. Eyewitnesses have said that Brown was compliant with police and was shot while he had his hands up. Police maintain that the 18-year-old had assaulted an officer and was reaching for the officer's gun. One thing clear, however, is that Brown's death follows a disturbingly common trend of black men being killed, often while unarmed and at the hands of police officers, security guards and vigilantes.

After news of Brown's death broke, media-watchers carefully followed the narratives that news outlets began crafting about the teenager and the incident that claimed his life. Wary of the controversy surrounding the media's depiction of Trayvon Martin -- the Florida teen killed in a high-profile case that led to the acquittal of neighborhood watchman George Zimmerman -- people on Twitter wondered, &quot;If they gunned me down, which picture would they use?&quot; Using the hashtag #IfTheyGunnedMeDown, users posted side-by-side photos, demonstrating the power that news outlets wield in portraying victims based on images they select.

On Monday, Twitter user LordSWVP tweeted out a photo driving home another point: Media treatment of black victims is often harsher than it is of whites suspected of crimes, including murder.

This makes the hashtag #IfTheyGunnedMeDown so powerful. It's sad that some people have taken it to another level. pic.twitter.com/oZnLDRRDhN&mdash; Sammie. &trade; (@LordSWVP) August 11, 2014


This is by no means standard media protocol, but it happens frequently, deliberately or not. News reports often headline claims from police or other officials that appear unsympathetic or dismissive of black victims. Other times, the headlines seem to suggest that black victims are to blame for their own deaths, engaging in what critics sometimes allege is a form of character assassination. When contrasted with media portrayal of white suspects and accused murderers, the differences are more striking. News outlets often choose to run headlines that exhibit an air of disbelief at an alleged white killer's supposed actions. Sometimes, they appear to go out of their way to boost the suspect's character, carrying quotes from relatives or acquaintances that often paint even alleged murderers in a positive light.

Here are a few examples:

WHITE SUSPECT



 That's how the Lubbock Avalanche-Journal chose to present the story of Amy Bishop, a former college professor who eventually pleaded guilty to killing three colleagues and wounding three others at a faculty meeting in 2010.

BLACK VICTIM



And that's the headline AL.com ran about the shooting death of a 25-year-old black man in Alabama earlier this year.

WHITE SUSPECT



This is how the Staten Island Advance covered the case of Eric Bellucci, a mentally ill New York man who allegedly killed his parents.

BLACK VICTIM



Meanwhile, NBC News ran this headline during ongoing coverage of the Trayvon Martin killing.

WHITE SUSPECT



This Fox News headline quoted friends shocked that 15-year-old Jared Michael Padgett had entered his high school heavily armed and killed a classmate, injured a teacher and took his own life.

BLACK VICTIM



But in Florida, this headline in the Ledger focused on a police account that made the death of a black 19-year-old seem somehow expected, or at least unsurprising.

WHITE SUSPECT



In the wake of the mass shooting in Santa Barbara, California, earlier this year, the Whittier Daily News offered a headline showing one man's disbelief that Elliot Rodger could have committed such a crime.

BLACK VICTIM



Earlier this month, the New York Daily News ran this headline, carrying comments by the Ohio attorney general that appeared to defend police after killing a black man at a Walmart.

WHITE SUSPECT



This was the headline given to an Associated Press story at Mlive.com about an Ohio teen who later pleaded guilty to a school shooting in which three students were killed and two were wounded.

BLACK VICTIM



But when an unarmed father of two was killed by a police officer while entering a vehicle that contained his own children, the Los Angeles Times served up this claim from officials.

WHITE SUSPECT



In 2008, 18-year-old Ryan Schallenberger was accused of plotting to bomb his South Carolina high school. Ohio's Chronicle Telegram wanted readers to know that he was a straight-A student, running an AP story with this headline.

BLACK VICTIM



And according to the Omaha World-Herald, this is what you needed to know about Julius B. Vaughn, a 19-year-old gunned down in Omaha last year:

WHITE SUSPECT



Kerri Ann Heffernan was charged in 2012 in a string of bank robberies and stores. This headline at Wicked Local wonders how she'd come so far from her days as a smart high school student.

BLACK VICTIM



Of 22-year-old black man Deon Sanders' killing in Ohio earlier this year, WKBN's headline said &quot;gang member,&quot; and that apparently was enough.",

   <script>
    (function($){ // no Conflict
    $(function() { // dom ready
    var socialSubSearch = $('#social-subscribe-search'),
        search = socialSubSearch.find('.search'),
        newsletter = socialSubSearch.find('.newsletters'),
        rollout = socialSubSearch.find('[data-fx="hover"]'),
        liContent = socialSubSearch.find('.content'),
        searchInput = search.find('.input-term'),
        searchText = search.find('.text');
        var searchcheck="Huffington Post Search";
        var checkInputContent = function(evt){
        var inputVal = searchInput.val();
        if (inputVal != searchcheck &amp;&amp; inputVal != "") {
            search.addClass('searching');
        } else {
            search.removeClass('searching');
        }
    };
    
    newsletter.find('.content').hover(
      function(){
        var inputVal = searchInput.val();
        if (inputVal != searchcheck &amp;&amp; inputVal != "") {
          search.removeClass('searching');
          searchText.text(inputVal.slice(0, 3) + '...');
        }
      },
      function(){
        var inputVal = searchInput.val();
        if (inputVal != searchcheck &amp;&amp; inputVal != "") {
          search.addClass('searching');
          searchText.text('Huffpost Search');
        }
      }
    );
    
    search.mouseout(checkInputContent);
    searchInput.blur(checkInputContent);
    
    // rollover effects
    liContent
      .on('mouseenter', function() {
        var that = $(this),
            thatParent = that.parent('li'),
            inputField = that.find('input[type="text"]');
    
        if(thatParent.data('fx') === 'hover') {
          thatParent.addClass('hover');
          inputField.focus();
        }
      })
      .on('mouseleave', function() {
            var that = $(this),
                thatParent = that.parent('li'),
                inputField = that.find('input[type="text"]');
                
            thatParent.removeClass('hover');
            inputField.blur();
          }); 
        // end liContent
    });
})(jQuery);
   </script>

            <a href="http://reddit.com/submit?url=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.huffingtonpost.com%2F2014%2F08%2F14%2Fmedia-black-victims_n_5673291.html&amp;title=When The Media Treats White Suspects And Killers Better Than Black Victims" target="chicklet" title="Share on Reddit">
             <span class="hidden">
              reddit
             </span>
            </a>
           </li>
          </ul>
         </section>
        </menu>
        <!-- Print Icon for Canada and Quebect verticals in permalink page -->
        <a class="print_btn print_common" href="javascript:window.print()" title="Print">
         <img alt="Print" height="17" src="http://www.huffingtonpost.com/images/v/print_icon.png" width="20"/>
        </a>
        <div style="clear:both">
        </div>
       </header>
       <!-- Article Text Body -->
       <div class="float_right padding_left_10">
       </div>
       <!-- Entry main text -->
       <div class="content" id="mainentrycontent">
        <div class="float_left">
         <!-- AD ads_sharebox_260x60 -->
         <div class="ad_share_box">
          <script type="text/javascript">
           if ( 'undefined' != typeof(HPAds.ad_sharebox_260x60_fix) ) {
              HPAds.ad_sharebox_260x60_fix();
            }
          </script>
         </div>
        </div>
        <!-- Entry Text -->
        <p>
         On the afternoon of Aug. 9, a police officer
         <a href="http://www.huffingtonpost.com/2014/08/09/ferguson-teen-police-shooting_n_5665305.html" target="_hplink">
          fatally shot an unarmed, black teenager, Michael Brown,
         </a>
         in Ferguson, Missouri. Details remain in dispute.
         <a href="http://www.nbcnews.com/storyline/michael-brown-shooting/michael-browns-friend-he-was-shot-animal-officer-n179501" target="_hplink">
          Eyewitnesses have said
         </a>
         that Brown was compliant with police and was shot while he had his hands up. Police maintain that the 18-year-old had assaulted an officer and was reaching for the officer's gun. One thing clear, however, is that Brown's death follows a disturbingly common trend of black men being killed, often while unarmed and at the hands of police officers, security guards and vigilantes.
        </p>
        <p>
         After news of Brown's death broke, media-watchers carefully followed the narratives that news outlets began crafting about the teenager and the incident that claimed his life. Wary of the
         <a href="http://news.yahoo.com/blogs/cutline/trayvon-martin-shooting-debate-over-photos-escalates-155103512.html" target="_hplink">
          controversy surrounding the media's depiction of Trayvon Martin
         </a>
         -- the Florida teen killed in a high-profile case that led to the acquittal of neighborhood watchman George Zimmerman -- people on Twitter wondered, "If they gunned me down, which picture would they use?" Using the
         <a href="http://www.huffingtonpost.com/2014/08/11/michael-brown-twitter_n_5668437.html" target="_hplink">
          hashtag #IfTheyGunnedMeDown, users posted
         </a>
         side-by-side photos, demonstrating the power that news outlets wield in portraying victims based on images they select.
        </p>
        <p>
         On Monday,
         <a href="https://twitter.com/LordSWVP/status/498892967231238144/photo/1" target="_hplink">
          Twitter user LordSWVP tweeted out a photo
         </a>
         driving home another point: Media treatment of black victims is often harsher than it is of whites suspected of crimes, including murder.
        </p>
        <blockquote class="twitter-tweet" lang="en">
         <p>
          This makes the hashtag
          <a href="https://twitter.com/hashtag/IfTheyGunnedMeDown?src=hash">
           #IfTheyGunnedMeDown
          </a>
          so powerful. It's sad that some people have taken it to another level.
          <a href="http://t.co/oZnLDRRDhN">
           pic.twitter.com/oZnLDRRDhN
          </a>
         </p>
         <p>
           Sammie.  (@LordSWVP)
          <a href="https://twitter.com/LordSWVP/statuses/498892967231238144">
           August 11, 2014
          </a>
         </p>
        </blockquote>
        <script async="" charset="utf-8" src="//platform.twitter.com/widgets.js">
        </script>
        <p>
         This is by no means standard media protocol, but it happens frequently, deliberately or not. News reports often headline claims from police or other officials that appear unsympathetic or dismissive of black victims. Other times, the headlines seem to suggest that black victims are to blame for their own deaths, engaging in what critics sometimes allege is a form of character assassination. When contrasted with media portrayal of white suspects and accused murderers, the differences are more striking. News outlets often choose to run headlines that exhibit an air of disbelief at an alleged white killer's supposed actions. Sometimes, they appear to go out of their way to boost the suspect's character, carrying quotes from relatives or acquaintances that often paint even alleged murderers in a positive light.
        </p>
        <p>
         Here are a few examples:
        </p>
        <center>
         <p>
         </p>
         <h3>
          <font color="EE2626">
           WHITE SUSPECT
          </font>
         </h3>
        </center>
        <p>
         <img alt="suspect 1" src="http://i.huffpost.com/gen/1963404/thumbs/o-SUSPECT-1-570.jpg?6"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <strong>
          <font color="787575" size="2">
           That's how the
           <a href="http://lubbockonline.com/stories/022110/loc_565688235.shtml" target="_hplink">
            Lubbock Avalanche-Journal chose to present
           </a>
           the story of Amy Bishop, a former college professor who eventually
           <a href="http://www.huffingtonpost.com/2012/09/12/amy-bishop-guilty_n_1876858.html" target="_hplink">
            pleaded guilty
           </a>
           to killing three colleagues and wounding three others at a faculty meeting in 2010.
          </font>
         </strong>
        </p>
        <center>
         <p>
         </p>
         <h3>
          <font color="EE2626">
           BLACK VICTIM
          </font>
         </h3>
        </center>
        <p>
         <img alt="victim 7" src="http://i.huffpost.com/gen/1963360/thumbs/o-VICTIM-7-570.jpg?6"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <strong>
          <font color="787575" size="2">
           And
           <a href="http://www.al.com/news/montgomery/index.ssf/2014/04/montgomerys_latest_homicide_vi.html" target="_hplink">
            that's the headline AL.com ran
           </a>
           about the shooting death of a 25-year-old black man in Alabama earlier this year.
          </font>
         </strong>
        </p>
        <center>
         <p>
         </p>
         <h3>
          <font color="EE2626">
           WHITE SUSPECT
          </font>
         </h3>
        </center>
        <p>
         <img alt="suspect 2" src="http://i.huffpost.com/gen/1962758/thumbs/o-SUSPECT-2-570.jpg?2"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <strong>
          <font color="787575" size="2">
           This is how the
           <a href="http://www.silive.com/southshore/index.ssf/2010/10/son_in_staten_island_murders_w.html" target="_hplink">
            Staten Island Advance covered
           </a>
           the case of Eric Bellucci, a mentally ill New York man who allegedly killed his parents.
          </font>
         </strong>
        </p>
        <center>
         <p>
         </p>
         <h3>
          <font color="EE2626">
           BLACK VICTIM
          </font>
         </h3>
        </center>
        <p>
         <img alt="trayvon" src="http://i.huffpost.com/gen/1964185/thumbs/o-TRAYVON-570.jpg?1"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <strong>
          <font color="787575" size="2">
           Meanwhile,
           <a href="http://usnews.nbcnews.com/_news/2012/03/26/10872124-trayvon-martin-was-suspended-three-times-from-school" target="_hplink">
            NBC News ran this headline
           </a>
           during ongoing coverage of the Trayvon Martin killing.
          </font>
         </strong>
        </p>
        <center>
         <p>
         </p>
         <h3>
          <font color="EE2626">
           WHITE SUSPECT
          </font>
         </h3>
        </center>
        <p>
         <img alt="suspect 3" src="http://i.huffpost.com/gen/1962765/thumbs/o-SUSPECT-3-570.jpg?2"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <strong>
          <font color="787575" size="2">
           This
           <a href="http://www.foxnews.com/us/2014/06/12/oregon-school-shooting-suspect-fascinated-with-guns-but-was-devoted-mormon-his/" target="_hplink">
            Fox News headline
           </a>
           quoted friends shocked that 15-year-old Jared Michael Padgett had entered his high school heavily armed and killed a classmate, injured a teacher and took his own life.
          </font>
         </strong>
        </p>
        <center>
         <p>
         </p>
         <h3>
          <font color="EE2626">
           BLACK VICTIM
          </font>
         </h3>
        </center>
        <p>
         <img alt="victim 6" src="http://i.huffpost.com/gen/1963357/thumbs/o-VICTIM-6-570.jpg?2"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <strong>
          <font color="787575" size="2">
           But in Florida,
           <a href="http://www.theledger.com/article/20140310/NEWS/140319988" target="_hplink">
            this headline in the Ledger
           </a>
           focused on a police account that made the death of a black 19-year-old seem somehow expected, or at least unsurprising.
          </font>
         </strong>
        </p>
        <center>
         <p>
         </p>
         <h3>
          <font color="EE2626">
           WHITE SUSPECT
          </font>
         </h3>
        </center>
        <p>
         <img alt="suspect 5" src="http://i.huffpost.com/gen/1962772/thumbs/o-SUSPECT-5-570.jpg?4"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <strong>
          <font color="787575" size="2">
           In the wake of the mass shooting in Santa Barbara, California, earlier this year, the
           <a href="http://www.whittierdailynews.com/general-news/20140525/santa-barbara-shooting-suspect-was-soft-spoken-polite-a-gentleman-ex-principal-says" target="_hplink">
            Whittier Daily News offered a headline
           </a>
           showing one man's disbelief that Elliot Rodger could have committed such a crime.
          </font>
         </strong>
        </p>
        <center>
         <p>
         </p>
         <h3>
          <font color="EE2626">
           BLACK VICTIM
          </font>
         </h3>
        </center>
        <p>
         <img alt="victim 1" src="http://i.huffpost.com/gen/1963167/thumbs/o-VICTIM-1-570.jpg?3"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <strong>
          <font color="787575" size="2">
           Earlier this month, the
           <a href="http://www.nydailynews.com/news/crime/police-kill-man-air-rifle-walmart-ohio-article-1.1895479#ixzz3AHJv8HRX" target="_hplink">
            New York Daily News ran this headline
           </a>
           , carrying comments by the Ohio attorney general that appeared to defend police after
           <a href="http://www.huffingtonpost.com/2014/08/11/john-crawford-iii_n_5669715.html" target="_hplink">
            killing a black man at a Walmart
           </a>
           .
          </font>
         </strong>
        </p>
        <center>
         <p>
         </p>
         <h3>
          <font color="EE2626">
           WHITE SUSPECT
          </font>
         </h3>
        </center>
        <p>
         <img alt="suspect 4" src="http://i.huffpost.com/gen/1962768/thumbs/o-SUSPECT-4-570.jpg?2"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <strong>
          <font color="787575" size="2">
           This was the
           <a href="http://www.mlive.com/news/us-world/index.ssf/2012/03/ohio_shooting_suspect_tj_lane.html" target="_hplink">
            headline given to an Associated Press story at Mlive.com
           </a>
           about an Ohio teen who later pleaded guilty to a school shooting in which three students were killed and two were wounded.
          </font>
         </strong>
        </p>
        <center>
         <p>
         </p>
         <h3>
          <font color="EE2626">
           BLACK VICTIM
          </font>
         </h3>
        </center>
        <p>
         <img alt="victim 4" src="http://i.huffpost.com/gen/1963185/thumbs/o-VICTIM-4-570.jpg?3"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <strong>
          <font color="787575" size="2">
           But when an unarmed father of two was killed by a police officer while entering a vehicle that contained his own children, the
           <a href="http://latimesblogs.latimes.com/lanow/2012/02/marine-shot-.html" target="_hplink">
            Los Angeles Times served up this claim
           </a>
           from officials.
          </font>
         </strong>
        </p>
        <center>
         <p>
         </p>
         <h3>
          <font color="EE2626">
           WHITE SUSPECT
          </font>
         </h3>
        </center>
        <p>
         <img alt="suspect 7" src="http://i.huffpost.com/gen/1962780/thumbs/o-SUSPECT-7-570.jpg?4"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <strong>
          <font color="787575" size="2">
           In 2008, 18-year-old Ryan Schallenberger was accused of plotting to bomb his South Carolina high school. Ohio's
           <a href="http://chronicle.northcoastnow.com/2008/04/21/straight-a-student-plots-to-bomb-high-school/" target="_hplink">
            Chronicle Telegram wanted readers to know
           </a>
           that he was a straight-A student, running an AP story with this headline.
          </font>
         </strong>
        </p>
        <center>
         <p>
         </p>
         <h3>
          <font color="EE2626">
           BLACK VICTIM
          </font>
         </h3>
        </center>
        <p>
         <img alt="victim 3" src="http://i.huffpost.com/gen/1963343/thumbs/o-VICTIM-3-570.jpg?5"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <strong>
          <font color="787575" size="2">
           And
           <a href="http://www.omaha.com/news/shooting-victim-had-many-run-ins-with-law/article_867c8b61-9a39-5b14-8c88-f5323058ff29.html" target="_hplink">
            according to the Omaha World-Herald
           </a>
           , this is what you needed to know about Julius B. Vaughn, a 19-year-old gunned down in Omaha last year:
          </font>
         </strong>
        </p>
        <center>
         <p>
         </p>
         <h3>
          <font color="EE2626">
           WHITE SUSPECT
          </font>
         </h3>
        </center>
        <p>
         <img alt="suspect 6" src="http://i.huffpost.com/gen/1962775/thumbs/o-SUSPECT-6-570.jpg?4"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <strong>
          <font color="787575" size="2">
           Kerri Ann Heffernan was charged in 2012 in a string of bank robberies and stores.
           <a href="http://www.wickedlocal.com/x1826358906/Bank-robbery-suspect-was-outstanding-Blue-Hills-student" target="_hplink">
            This headline at Wicked Local
           </a>
           wonders how she'd come so far from her days as a smart high school student.
          </font>
         </strong>
        </p>
        <center>
         <p>
         </p>
         <h3>
          <font color="EE2626">
           BLACK VICTIM
          </font>
         </h3>
        </center>
        <p>
         <img alt="victim 2" src="http://i.huffpost.com/gen/1963174/thumbs/o-VICTIM-2-570.jpg?3"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <strong>
          <font color="787575" size="2">
           Of 22-year-old black man Deon Sanders' killing in Ohio earlier this year,
           <a href="http://wkbn.com/2014/06/18/police-warren-shooting-victim-was-gang-member/" target="_hplink">
            WKBN's headline
           </a>
           said "gang member," and that apparently was enough.
          </font>
         </strong>
        </p>

         <script>
          // Restrict Most Popular title to 2 lines
(function() {
if (!window.jQuery) { return; }
var $mpt = jQuery('.mp_title');
if ($mpt.length == 0) return;
function numLines($elem) {
  lh = parseFloat($elem.css('line-height').replace('px', ''));
  return Math.round($elem.height()/lh);
}
for (i=0; i&lt;10 &amp;&amp; numLines($mpt)&gt;2; i++) {
  $mpt.css('font-size', '-=1');
}
})();
         </script>
